<span id="freeTextContainer33317656388359757">On the veranda of a great New Orleans house, now faded, a mute and fragile woman sits rocking. And the witching hour begins ... <br /><br />Demonstrating once again her gift for spellbinding storytelling and the creation of legend, Anne Rice makes real for us a great dynasty of witches --- a family given to poetry and incest, to murder and philosophy, a family that over the ages is it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText33317656388359757">On the veranda of a great New Orleans house, now faded, a mute and fragile woman sits rocking. And the witching hour begins ... <br /><br />Demonstrating once again her gift for spellbinding storytelling and the creation of legend, Anne Rice makes real for us a great dynasty of witches --- a family given to poetry and incest, to murder and philosophy, a family that over the ages is itself haunted by a powerful, dangerous, and seductive being. A hypnotic novel of witchcraft and the occult across four centuries. The Witching Hour could only have been written by the spellbinding bestselling author of <em>The Vampire Chronicles.</em></span>

          });
        });
      $('edition_436044').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script></div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_15032641">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15032641" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/740952-elise-jensen" class="left imgcol" title="Elise Jensen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289706029p2/740952.jpg" alt="Elise Jensen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15032641?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/740952-elise-jensen" class="user" title="Elise Jensen">Elise Jensen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour" title="Paperback 9780099471424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/740952-elise-jensen?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15032641">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8905217148283716015">I actually quite enjoyed this book up until the very end, when I felt like the main female character just had some sort of weird personality seizure and did something that the character as you've come to know her just wouldn't have done. It just made it seem poorly written to me, like Ms. Rice decided in the last 10 pages or so that it was going to have a sequel after all when she had been intending from the beginning for it to be a one-book story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17160821159409665901">I got this book for Christmas that year. This was my first ever Anne Rice book, and it was about a year after Interview With A Vampire came out as a movie with Brad Pitt, Christian Slater and Tom Cruise. I was blown away people. If you like a story, like <a title="Gone With The Wind by Margaret Mitchell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18405.Gone_With_The_Wind">Gone With the Wind</a> on crack, no seriously, epic like that, except VERY ADULT (don't let your tweens get their hands on this one Mom's and Dad's!), but such an addicting read that you may just get fired for calling in sick over it.<br /><br />This was far an</span>

      <a href="/user/show/1084654-liisa" class="user" title="Liisa">Liisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=vampire-werewolves-witches-mystical" class="actionLinkLite">vampire-werewolves-witches-mystical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1084654-liisa?shelf=trilogies-and-series" class="actionLinkLite">trilogies-and-series</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer36811575'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36811575">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14243187104202500599">What a queer little book (although at 1207 pages, little isn't the right word)! This was my first attempt at <em>Anne Rice</em> and I fear it might well be my last.<br /><br />Halfway through <strong>"The Witching Hour"</strong>, I was absolutely enthralled. I loved the idea of The Talamasca. At that stage of the story, I would have loved knowing it was a real organisation and applied for a job. I revelled in learning the entire Mayfair history. <em>Anne Rice</em> has a gift for choosing the words that bring it all to life. I could imagine t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14243187104202500599">What a queer little book (although at 1207 pages, little isn't the right word)! This was my first attempt at <em>Anne Rice</em> and I fear it might well be my last.<br /><br />Halfway through <strong>"The Witching Hour"</strong>, I was absolutely enthralled. I loved the idea of The Talamasca. At that stage of the story, I would have loved knowing it was a real organisation and applied for a job. I revelled in learning the entire Mayfair history. <em>Anne Rice</em> has a gift for choosing the words that bring it all to life. I could imagine the house on First Street and see everything as the characters walk through the Garden District.<br /><br />So why only one star? Firstly, I thought it was too long. I love books &amp; reading and don't shy away from a challenge but I felt it just took too long to get to a disappointing ending. And that really is the crux of my complaint. How it all ends. In a word, pitifully.<br /><br />Rowan, the all-powerful 13th witch in the Mayfair Dynasty &amp; destiny, so completely consumed in her eternal love for Michael - gives up, betrays Michael and helps Lasher? Please. For me, it not only belittled her character (and relationship with Michael) but made a mockery of it. None of it rang true. After wading through this, all I am left with is a feeling of being cheated.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14243187104202500599">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_65759559">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65759559" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2583489-derek-oberg" class="left imgcol" title="Derek Oberg"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1249104224p2/2583489.jpg" alt="Derek Oberg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/65759559?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 01, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2583489-derek-oberg" class="user" title="Derek Oberg">Derek Oberg</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/333716.The_Witching_Hour" title="Hardcover 9780394587868" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Most</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer65759559">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15947979491033256814">One of my top 3 favorite novels of all time. Anne Rice gets a bad rap for being pure shlock, but what most people who haven't read her don't realize is that she is <em>obsessed</em> with history. She studies a particular time period, learns everything she can about it, and then creates characters and sticks them in it. She rarely disappoints me. And her prose is beautiful. You can sit down to read and realize that 2 hours have passed having not even noticed.<br /><br />This book is about a woman named Rowan Mayfair,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15947979491033256814">One of my top 3 favorite novels of all time. Anne Rice gets a bad rap for being pure shlock, but what most people who haven't read her don't realize is that she is <em>obsessed</em> with history. She studies a particular time period, learns everything she can about it, and then creates characters and sticks them in it. She rarely disappoints me. And her prose is beautiful. You can sit down to read and realize that 2 hours have passed having not even noticed.<br /><br />This book is about a woman named Rowan Mayfair, who was given up for adoption at birth. She has lived a very normal, successful life and become a doctor, knowing nothing of her birth family or the circumstances of her adoption.<br /><br />...And then her birth mother in New Orleans dies. Suddenly Rowan finds herself haunted by an apparition that she cannot explain. She is approached by an old man named Aaron Lightner who tells her that he is with an orginazition called the Talamasca. He explains that they exist to watch and study paranormal and supernatural events, but do not interfere. They have been watching the Mayfair family for hundreds of years. (After this book, the Talamasca was merged into Rice's primary ongoing serial, "The Vampire Chronicles.")<br /><br />Aaron presents her with the file on her family, and the narrative breaks away for a good 300 pages to tell the tale of an ancient coven of witches, reaching back as far as the 1600's. The familiar of the Mayfair family is a very powerful spirit named Lasher. He is passed down to the first-born daughter of each generation. Now that her mother is dead, Lasher has moved on to Rowan.<br /><br />Rowan decides to head to New Orleans to attend her mother's funeral and meet the family. VERY thrilling, exciting, white-knuckled reading ensues.<br /><br />This is the first book in "The Lives of the Mayfair Witches," a series which originally spanned only 3 books. But when Rice decided that it was time to end all of her ongoing serials, she merged these characters with those from the Vampire Chronicles and ended them both together.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15947979491033256814">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_201716153">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201716153" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn" class="left imgcol" title="Aoibhínn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451237485p2/5799885.jpg" alt="Aoibhínn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/201716153?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn" class="user" title="Aoibhínn">Aoibhínn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour" title="Paperback 9780099471424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=physical-books" class="actionLinkLite">physical-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer201716153">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8497957394317508986">The Mayfair's are an extremely powerful and wealthy family, in each generation there is a chosen one, a witch, who inherits not only the family home and money, but supernatural powers and an evil entity, named Lasher, who only has one aim – to become human again. <br /><br /><em>The Witching Hour</em> is an extremely long novel, 1207 pages, but don't let that put you off reading as once you open the first page you soon find yourself completely absorbed in the chilling tale of the Mayfair Witches. This novel has a sp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8497957394317508986">The Mayfair's are an extremely powerful and wealthy family, in each generation there is a chosen one, a witch, who inherits not only the family home and money, but supernatural powers and an evil entity, named Lasher, who only has one aim – to become human again. <br /><br /><em>The Witching Hour</em> is an extremely long novel, 1207 pages, but don't let that put you off reading as once you open the first page you soon find yourself completely absorbed in the chilling tale of the Mayfair Witches. This novel has a spellbinding, engrossing, well-written tale with complex and mysterious characters. There are plenty of compelling twists and turns in the plot to keep you interested and the suspense is drawn out to perfection. The novel is completely unpredictable, I found the ending to be quite a shock! <br /><br />The settings of each generation of the family, from the plantations on Haiti to the modern day gothic mansion in New Orleans, are so richly described that you can easily imagine yourself there in those places. In fact, I loved all Anne Rice's vivid descriptions of New Orleans and the house on First Street, I found this really added to the intensity of the story.<br /><br />There was a section in the middle, of about 300 pages or more, describing the history of the Mayfair family, the whole 12 generations of the family! I found this section quite tiresome and entirely too long, which is why I'm giving this novel four stars instead of five. I wished the author had shortened this section. <br /><br />The characters were all quite complex, fascinating and well-developed. Anne Rice spent a lot of time explaining the motives behind her characters and why they react the way they do to situations in the novel. It also made me feel that I knew each individual character very well. Throughout the novel, I felt myself feeling both sympathy and anger towards the character of Rowan.<br /><br />Beware, if you try to read this novel in paperback format, your eyes and wrists will be sore for about a week! <br /><br /><br />Four stars!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8497957394317508986">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_163876238">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163876238" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4490376-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346056033p2/4490376.jpg" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/163876238?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4490376-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10221122-the-witching-hour" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=read-regifted" class="actionLinkLite">read-regifted</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=reviewed-snarky" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-snarky</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=zzz-2013-leftovers-completed" class="actionLinkLite">zzz-2013-leftovers-completed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=zzz-2013" class="actionLinkLite">zzz-2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4490376-sarah?shelf=whingy-noodle-boner" class="actionLinkLite">whingy-noodle-boner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer163876238">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14656718306863029509"><strong>Warning: SPOILERS. And gifs. Lots of both, actually.</strong><br /><br /><br />I don't even know how to summarize what I've just finished. It's like trying to tell someone what happens in a George RR Martin novel. You might try to list item by item, but everything is woven with everything else &amp; there's no way to distinguish in the grand scheme. <em>"Oh, y'know. Stuff happens. People threaten each other. People fight. People die. People have sex. More stuff happens. More people fight. More people die. The end."</em><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563244ra/5036826.gif" /><br />(Sorry, Rob</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14656718306863029509"><strong>Warning: SPOILERS. And gifs. Lots of both, actually.</strong><br /><br /><br />I don't even know how to summarize what I've just finished. It's like trying to tell someone what happens in a George RR Martin novel. You might try to list item by item, but everything is woven with everything else &amp; there's no way to distinguish in the grand scheme. <em>"Oh, y'know. Stuff happens. People threaten each other. People fight. People die. People have sex. More stuff happens. More people fight. More people die. The end."</em><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563244ra/5036826.gif" /><br />(Sorry, Robb.)<br /><br />Anyway.<br /><br />Before I get to what cheesed me off, let me say that the middle third of this book was great. I absolutely loved the family history portion of this novel -- the compendium of sources &amp; snippets relating to the Mayfair family through several hundred years. I would've happily read a complete novel about those people &amp; their fucked-up family dynamic. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the long-running cycle of Mayfair Witches seemed almost secondary to the primary plot -- a strange thing to say, yes, given that the series is called "The Mayfair Chronicles." But there it is. Rather than spend more time with Charlotte, Deborah, Carlotta, Stella, Julien, &amp; everyone else, it's painfully apparent that their lives &amp; misadventures are leading to Rowan Mayfair &amp; her boyfriend, Michael Curry, as their lives are woven into the Evul Plans of a very determined demon...spirit...thing named Lasher.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563244ra/5036827.gif" /><br /><br />Before I get to Rowan &amp; Michael, let's talk about Lasher. What IS Lasher? After 1000 pages, he's still not clearly defined. He's an immortal being with intelligence that was called into Earthly existence by a simpleton witch &amp; over the centuries he's learned to manipulate mortals &amp; breed them together in his ultimate quest -- that is, he wants to give himself a body. One would think that makes him mortal, but apparently not. (Just one of several logic gaps. Ignore them as needed.) At any rate, Lasher has been interbreeding one family because he looks into the future &amp; sees one specific witch (Rowan) as his door into the world of sensational experience. As powerful as other witches have been -- especially Charlotte, Julien, &amp; Mary Beth -- they lack Rowan's conceptions of modernity &amp; medicine, which are what make her so strong.<br /><br />Or something. It's a really long-term Cunning Plan(tm).<br /><br />Yeah, that's right. The demon...spirit...thing has a Cunning Plan(tm), &amp; it's worthy of Gray Eagle himself. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563244ra/5036828.gif" /><br /><br />As for how Lasher's final transformation is to be accomplished...well, it was somewhat nonsensical. It involves Lasher fusing himself with the fetus in Rowan's body, which then emerges in a bloody scene of horrific birthing (though still vague in detail). This mutant spawn is born with a giant head &amp; limbs that grow into full man-size within minutes, &amp; Rowan has to lay her hands on his body &amp; make sure his organs develop properly so he can actually live &amp; breathe &amp; have sex &amp; walk around. The whole thing is beyond serious recount. Clearly the author was going for some kind of Frankenstein tribute, but it didn't work. By this point -- somewhere around page 1015 -- I just didn't give a fuck. And who's to blame for my not caring? Rowan &amp; Michael. <br /><br />Michael is a classically-styled nice guy, but that's ALL he is. <em>His niceness is boring as hell.</em> He's built like a firefighter &amp; uber-sensitive -- as in, he cries at the beauty of Christmas &amp; finds poetry in restoring old houses &amp; weeps inside at the ecstasy of making love with Rowan. (Yes, really.) But despite my personal feelings toward this sort of hero, Michael's woobie behavior might have been tolerable had the heroine made up for it. <br /><br />Nope. Didn't happen.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563244ra/5036829.gif" /><br /><br />Rowan has mysterious healing powers, but she can also kill people with her mind. That sounds great in theory -- except she's a moo of the first order. She judges constantly, looks down on people for having Feelz, &amp; drives like a maniac because she's just that awesome. But she's so very, very lonely &amp; deprived of emotional companionship &amp; <em>of course</em> her powers scare her, but she's determined to use them for good &amp; healing &amp; compassion toward the little people of the universe who are human enough to need medical care, and...<br /><br />Excuse me for disparaging her self-righteous spews of whinge. *chortle* At the end of the book, after vowing repeatedly &amp; at great length to destroy Lasher at her first opportunity, what does she do? She falls into the first mental trap Lasher sets, abandons the great love of her life that she's been banging on about for the entire novel, lets a demonic spirit seduce her, falls in love with said demonic spirit, heals his freaky fetus body because she can't bear to destroy life, &amp; runs away with him to hide in Europe &amp; do medical research on his cellular tissues. Seriously?<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563770ra/5037489.gif" /><br /><br />So what happened to the Mayfair Witches storyline -- the one about a family of occultists that do witchy things to each other &amp; have a ghost haunting their family? Looking back, I can only say the book's true focus wasn't on witchcraft. I wanted to read a 1000-page book about an inbred line of witches...but that's not what I got. Instead I found a 400-page family history &amp; a 600-page metaphysical sci-fi adaptation of the <em>The Omen</em>. The result was a book that felt like two different concepts forced into one unwieldy whole -- not to mention the book was 300 pages too long. o_O<br /><br />3.5 stars. The family compendium was quite interesting, but the rest was a borderline snooze.<br /><br /><br />To conclude, here's a picture of Robb holding an armload of puppies. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381563245ra/5036830.gif" /><br /><br />...I feel better already.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14656718306863029509">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2210315">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer904477124058694016">When I got to the end of this thick book, after having read hundreds of lukewarm pages, and found that it basically said "to be continued," I was pretty pissed off. If the book had been mine and not one I had borrowed from a friend, I would have tossed it across the room. That was when I decided that I would never again buy an Anne Rice book. I haven't.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192923036">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16075123603667076454">Review is tainted by romance.<br /><br />When my man and I first moved into the Garden District last summer (while I was still a bartender) we moved into a pristine apartment with a gallery balcony which overlooked Chestnut street. Left in our room in an otherwise pristine apartment was a box of clutter left by the previous tenant. She left spoons, a rubber ducky, a hideous vase and five Anne Rice novels. <br /><br />I spent most of the summer mornings on the balcony reading the Mayfair witches series, starting with Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16075123603667076454">Review is tainted by romance.<br /><br />When my man and I first moved into the Garden District last summer (while I was still a bartender) we moved into a pristine apartment with a gallery balcony which overlooked Chestnut street. Left in our room in an otherwise pristine apartment was a box of clutter left by the previous tenant. She left spoons, a rubber ducky, a hideous vase and five Anne Rice novels. <br /><br />I spent most of the summer mornings on the balcony reading the Mayfair witches series, starting with The Witching Hour. Under the shade of the magnolia tree next to our balcony I could actually see "the Mayfair House" from my window - the house that Anne Rice used to own when she wrote the series on Chestnut and First. A perfect way to spend the summer. So cliche, so wonderful.<br /><br />No balcony at my new place in Central City, but from my gallery windows I can see the bar that the Wild Magnolia Mardi Gras Indians practice and leave from on Mardi Gras morning and on St. Joseph's Day. Still a winner, just need a matching book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_133680368">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133680368" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4619796-geek-lee" class="left imgcol" title="Geek Lee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291511315p2/4619796.jpg" alt="Geek Lee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/133680368?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4619796-geek-lee" class="user" title="Geek Lee">Geek Lee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour" title="Paperback 9780099471424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer133680368'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer133680368">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8289533008288052853">Be Warned. Thar be major SPOILERS ahead!<br /><br />All and all, I loved this tale of a family with generations of witches. The witches are so interesting and seductive. Their "spirit", Lasher, is an enigma who does both good and bad things to the Mayfair witches. Anne Rice gave just enough information to keep me unsure but I always felt as though he was calling the shots with the witches, as early as Deborah. The Mayfair witches are free spirits who rarely conform to the norms of the day. The current witch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8289533008288052853">Be Warned. Thar be major SPOILERS ahead!<br /><br />All and all, I loved this tale of a family with generations of witches. The witches are so interesting and seductive. Their "spirit", Lasher, is an enigma who does both good and bad things to the Mayfair witches. Anne Rice gave just enough information to keep me unsure but I always felt as though he was calling the shots with the witches, as early as Deborah. The Mayfair witches are free spirits who rarely conform to the norms of the day. The current witch, Dr Rowan Mayfair, is a neurosurgeon who is on the cutting edge of genetic experimentation, a controversial topic for many.<br /><br />We see the story for a large part from the Talamasca’s POV so I am on the fence about whether the witches really had powers other than being able to see Lasher. There is a big fuss made of one witch's ability to make millions of dollars but Lasher tells Rowan he was the one who told ALL the witches where and when to invest. I'm still not sure what these witches can do -- this is very underdeveloped – and I can’t help thinking it would have been extremely helpful to hear some stories from the witches themselves. <br /><br />As it turn out Lasher was manipulating the witches in order to achieve his goal. We are never told about whether they realize he was lying and controlling them so I assume they didn’t know. Lasher turns out to be much more powerful than I expected. I mean, he was omniscient! He killed and had sex without the slightest remorse in order to become human. I suspect he possessed the witches frequently to create the incestuous relationships that formed the genes he needed from the Mayfair babies and that they did not do this of their own free will. Again, I can only assume this.<br /><br />Carlotta is a horribly twisted character. I thought her bitter cruelty came from being jealous of NOT being a witch so I was surprised to learn she WAS one. Interesting dichotomy to have her use her power to keep Lasher away from her while all the others use their power to keep Lasher with them. While I think she is the only truly "evil" witch, I have to admit, she had it right when it came to handling Lasher. And it is interesting to note that while Lasher is very powerful, he is the first to acknowledge he has made mistakes and we see one or two times Carlotta has tricked “the trickster”.<br /><br />The second drowning scene of Michael Curry, Rowan’s husband, was amazing. I could envision it so vividly and it seemed so morbidly fascinating that I wanted it to last much longer. All the Mayfair witches running around -- "frozen" to look as they did at the time of their death. All waiting for Lasher to bring them back to life and arguing over who goes first. I loved it!!! I wanted this to be the reality and not that Lasher was once again tricking Michael with another mind game. (Although I really like the idea of hell being your worst fears and not generic “brimstone and fire”) Anyway, this was a great scene for me.<br /><br />I found the ending anti-climatic. In fact the climax for me seems to be when Michael nearly drowns for a second time and while I loved the scene, it didn’t feel as though that should be such a strong scene while the real climax - the showdown between Rowan and Lasher - was so weak. With Lasher's birth happening "off screen" and Rowan trying to trick him to kill him so completely underdeveloped, I found this is a weak finale to the centuries old story. By the time of his birth on Christmas day (ridiculously cheesy, imho), Rowan has morphed from a strong, angry witch into a spineless, frightened girl. And she is the only one I am sure actually had "powers". Very unsatisfying. <br /><br />The ending was too soft and predictable. I wanted a stronger bang. Rowan leaves with Lasher – seemingly of her own free will – after being completely seduced and tricked by him. He told her she would have to choose between him and Michael and it seems as if she has. Michael is recovering from his near drowning at the house on First Street and the other Mayfairs are all convinced that everything is as it was meant to be. In fact, Michael wonders if witches are even real in the last pages of the book. No real push to read the sequels, to be honest. Although I am still wondering about those “witches”.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8289533008288052853">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5612357577004206245"> Engrossing from the first paragraph. Anne Rice is best known for her book, "Interview With the Vampire," but she SHOULD be best known for this. <br /> This is an epic novel that follows the lives of the Mayfair witches through generations, time and place. Eerie, magical, and mysterious. Characters are woven into an intricate and mesmerizing plot. Beautiful descriptive writing. <br /> I was chilled to the bone and genuinely scared during nearly every chapter, but addicted like nothing else. Stayed up way past my bedtime with this one. Or was it because I was too scared to go to sleep? ;)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9023089206954528107">this book is bad in so many ways. the most offensive being her erotic descriptions of incest and child sexual abuse activities. she writes these as steamy harlequin romance moments with no alluding to the wrongness and damage these activities and crimes truly are in real life. it's as if she champions them as some great sexual experiences. that in and of itself is enough for me to hate a book. i have zero respect for her as person. that being said, and those parts aside, the beginning of the boo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9023089206954528107">this book is bad in so many ways. the most offensive being her erotic descriptions of incest and child sexual abuse activities. she writes these as steamy harlequin romance moments with no alluding to the wrongness and damage these activities and crimes truly are in real life. it's as if she champions them as some great sexual experiences. that in and of itself is enough for me to hate a book. i have zero respect for her as person. that being said, and those parts aside, the beginning of the book is interesting and i liked it a lot plotwise and characterwise, but when she starts to delve into the history of the mayfair witches her characters become 2 dimensional cutouts that are really lame. all that matters is that they're good looking, charming and incestuous, sometimes being very inappropriate with children as i earlier stated. it's this same lame plot over and over again with different mayfair witches for literally hundreds of pages. i just can't plow through it all to get back to the part of the story i liked which does resurface at the end. i also find her representation of the black slaves racist. boring and gross and shamefully inappropriate at times. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2734480695715610116">I always hated vampire/witch stories but my honors English teacher in high school recommended this book to me for our final paper. Its about 1000 pages long so I used the first 500 hundred and literally fell in love. Since then I have read the book about five times. I LOVE IT. It centers around a wealthy family living in New Orleans, there is a spirit that follows one woman in every generation and the story follows the spirit from its conception. It is a really interesting, complex novel with ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2734480695715610116">I always hated vampire/witch stories but my honors English teacher in high school recommended this book to me for our final paper. Its about 1000 pages long so I used the first 500 hundred and literally fell in love. Since then I have read the book about five times. I LOVE IT. It centers around a wealthy family living in New Orleans, there is a spirit that follows one woman in every generation and the story follows the spirit from its conception. It is a really interesting, complex novel with many layers- it is not just a witch craft story but one about family and love and history.</span>

This by far was the best!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5648839814750174256"> This book stinks. Anne Rice wrote really good vampire books, but the Feast of All Saints was dreadful and I couldn't finish. Her book about the childhood of Christ was horribly slow and boring. The Witching Hour goes on and on and on. It is as boring as real life. You just wait for something to happen.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5648839814750174256"> This book stinks. Anne Rice wrote really good vampire books, but the Feast of All Saints was dreadful and I couldn't finish. Her book about the childhood of Christ was horribly slow and boring. The Witching Hour goes on and on and on. It is as boring as real life. You just wait for something to happen. Every few pages she gets around to saying something about someone who may or may not be a witch. <br /><br /> The narrative runs sort of like, "In 1954 one of our investigators talked to a maid who lived down the street. She said that once she totally freaked out when she saw a man talking with the Mayfair girl in her yard. There have been several similar reports from this time period gathered from various sources that say similar things. Records also indicate that this girl got expelled from two schools during this time period. This strong evidence had lead some of my colleagues to conclude that she is most definitely a witch... And this person begat that person. And that person begat that person. And the other person begat so-and so... Person A lived a very quiet life in which nothing happened. Person B lived a life of sin and scandal, but was not really a witch. Person C was a powerful witch but never cast any spells. Person D was probably a witch, but there is no sound evidence. Person E is some random cousin who really has nothing to do with the story or with witches and could have been safely left out of the book... Now we turn the the period that covers the 1960's."<br /><br /> I know that the book has really lost my respect and attention when I start skimming or even skipping pages to get to where something is going on.</span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer95061063">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6724054943381352567">Did not like this book. Her description skills are beautiful, which drew me in initially (plus I was looking for a book that would take me longer than a day to read, and at over a thousand pages...) You can SEE and FEEL what she says, like your in the room with her looking and touching her characters and environments. So I gave it a star for that.<br />However. How do you write over six hundred pages without touching on a story plot? I was kind of entranced by the huge history she gave the family, but</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6724054943381352567">Did not like this book. Her description skills are beautiful, which drew me in initially (plus I was looking for a book that would take me longer than a day to read, and at over a thousand pages...) You can SEE and FEEL what she says, like your in the room with her looking and touching her characters and environments. So I gave it a star for that.<br />However. How do you write over six hundred pages without touching on a story plot? I was kind of entranced by the huge history she gave the family, but I realized on around page six hundred she hadnt really set any kind of plot. Around page nine hundred, this was far more disconcerning, and I was wondering how she'd get to it in time. And then the ending...okay, I hated the ending. I suppose, reading this book as metaphorical, which hidden meaning and questions about society and how it was formed, this book might be good. I was kind of looking for an enthralling history/thriller about witches however, and this lady managed to write out seven hundred pages of backstory, with a semi-fantastical feel to her world, then shove the whole damn story into science fiction at the end. I re-read the scene about ten times before I skimmed through to the end. I also didnt like how her charactger is supposedly stronger and smarter than everyone else, and in the end she kind of just decides to throw a "just kidding just kidding, shes not really that smart or strong"...if you like sci fi and a LOT of backstory, this is an interesting read. I will just never read it again.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13618313667870981990">Whew! Made it!<br />I mean I managed to remain mostly sane while taking over 2 weeks to read this book.<br />I slept, ate and worked. When I first started Anne Rice's, The Witching Hour, I recognized the danger I faced to do nothing but read this 1200 page book from cover to cover in one sitting!   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13618313667870981990">Whew! Made it!<br />I mean I managed to remain mostly sane while taking over 2 weeks to read this book.<br />I slept, ate and worked. When I first started Anne Rice's, The Witching Hour, I recognized the danger I faced to do nothing but read this 1200 page book from cover to cover in one sitting! I would have hurt myself!<br /><br />In my humble opinion, Anne Rice is the greatest living author of good and evil. OK, I know she and I both are a little bit old fashioned now!<br /><br />Rowan, the leading lady, is an brilliant neurosurgeon; but also has the power to kill with her mind. She was adopted; then finds she's super rich with a huge family. It turns out she's the 13th witch in a long line of Mayfair witches and is the "doorway" to some unknown. She falls in love with Michael, a hunk of man with psychic powers. Michael tries to decipher the scholars of the Talamasca Files on the MayFair Witches and the meaning of his lover being this 13th doorway.<br /><br />This is a big read. If you have to have a happy ending, stop reading on page 913! Enjoy the beautiful people, scenery and history of the Occult. Just pretend the book ends with Rowan and Michael living happily ever after with their perfect child in their beautiful refurbished First Street mansion and sailing on their yacht, Sweet Christine, off their beach house on the gulf!<br /><br />I'm going to have to take a year off before I read Lasher, the sequel!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer175186018">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10999318500528314611">I tried to pick this up about early high school time. Anne Rice was and is a hard sell for me, I am in that minority of people who never cared at all about vampires. However, she wrote a couple other books that I read so I figured with this one being about witches I would stand to enjoy it. Witches and magic were much more of a draw for me even in a book of mammoth size. So I started this book and delved into the history of the Mayfair family/women. And holy hell. I couldn't get past the family</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10999318500528314611">I tried to pick this up about early high school time. Anne Rice was and is a hard sell for me, I am in that minority of people who never cared at all about vampires. However, she wrote a couple other books that I read so I figured with this one being about witches I would stand to enjoy it. Witches and magic were much more of a draw for me even in a book of mammoth size. So I started this book and delved into the history of the Mayfair family/women. And holy hell. I couldn't get past the family history. It was so drawn out and I found it boring. I kept waiting for plot but instead only got family trees. I returned the book to the library and never looked back.<br /><br />Only now as I looked up this book to write the review do I see that it is a trilogy... even more incentive to let sleeping dogs lie.<br /><br />Recommendation advice: do not pick up this book just because you like magic or witches. If you like family histories, generational sagas, New Orleans setting... then I would recommend this book to you.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_14816067">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14816067" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/866070-erin" class="left imgcol" title="Erin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1286557158p2/866070.jpg" alt="Erin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14816067?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/866070-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour" title="Paperback 9780099471424" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14816067">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14393846635290497244">I read this book back in High School. I loved the whole Mayfair witches series. The first in the Mayfair Witches series, The Witching Hour introduces the fictional Mayfair family of New Orleans, generations of male and female witches. This tight-knit and deeply connected family, where a death of one strengthens the others with his/her knowledge. One Mayfair witch per generation is also designated to receive the powers of "the man," known as Lasher. Lasher gives the witches gifts, excites them, a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14393846635290497244">I read this book back in High School. I loved the whole Mayfair witches series. The first in the Mayfair Witches series, The Witching Hour introduces the fictional Mayfair family of New Orleans, generations of male and female witches. This tight-knit and deeply connected family, where a death of one strengthens the others with his/her knowledge. One Mayfair witch per generation is also designated to receive the powers of "the man," known as Lasher. Lasher gives the witches gifts, excites them, and protects them. Unsure as to exactly what this spirit is, the Mayfair clan knows him variously as a protector, a god-like figure, a sexual being, and the image of death. Lasher's current witch is Deirdre, who lies catatonic from psycological shock treatments.<br /><br />Deirdre's daughter, Rowan, has been spirited away from this "evil" and has happily become a neurosurgeon and has an uncanny gift to see the intent behind the facade. Rowan also has a gift few doctors possess--she can heal cells. Yet, though she uses it to save lives, she also fears that she hs caused several deaths. She rescues Michael from drowning. Michael then develops some extraordinary powers that compel him to seek New Orleans and to seek Rowan. He finds both, and pulls the tale closer together by meeting people connected to the Mayfair family who now fear Rowan because she is the first Mayfair who can kill without Lasher's help.<br /><br />Michael dives into learning the history of the Mayfair witches: Deborah, Charlotte, Mary Beth, Stella, Antha, and many others across hundreds of years and three continents. When Michael looks up from his reading, he learns that Rowan has come to New Orleans to attend her mother's funeral. Rowan learns of her family history, her ancestral home in shambles, and Lasher waiting for the next one. Rowan dedicates herself to stopping Lasher's reign. Michael too has his own mission, but it is foggy and unclear to him. But Lasher is seductively powerful and Rowan's gifts offer him the opportunity to achieve his ultimate goal.<br /><br />The only warning I would give on these books is that they have a couple of pretty sexual parts, so if that bothers you, then I would pass.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14393846635290497244">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5080548639595412698">Okay so starting sagas now and to give me a larger challenge and this was 1026 page monster was my first endeavor..what can I say it is an engrossing and absorbing read that will take you away to a whole confusing, strange but entirely new place...Okay so its a saga of witches, women who call upon magic to conjure up spirits--in the family this story revolves around the Mayfairs witches from the beginning of about the sixteenth century to basically nineties present.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5080548639595412698">Okay so starting sagas now and to give me a larger challenge and this was 1026 page monster was my first endeavor..what can I say it is an engrossing and absorbing read that will take you away to a whole confusing, strange but entirely new place...Okay so its a saga of witches, women who call upon magic to conjure up spirits--in the family this story revolves around the Mayfairs witches from the beginning of about the sixteenth century to basically nineties present. It is a tough book to get through with all the histories, family names, lineages, flashbacks, and foreshadowing it can get difficult..this book took me about an unheard of three weeks only because of its size and complexity--I wanted to understand this book so I could go on and as much as I could I think I have..its perplexing, all the action happens at the end, when you are ready to give up but the whole journey is worth it, once you get it, recognize names and people and relationships past and present it is a great read..I only recommend it for those wanting a challenge, something to get engrossed in and a way to spend your nights for a few weeks..</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer583843246">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17044135329104358979">Although I've read this before it was still a good book to re-read. There is so much history of New Orleans written, with about the first 700 pages mostly detailing the background of the Mayfair witches. The main characters are Rowan Mayfair and Michael curry, with the ghost Lasher.<br /><br />Although long at just over 1200 pages, the book is never slow moveing. The characters are interesting, and with some you really like. Lots of the very large Mayfair family are great such as Beartrice, but in Carlotta</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17044135329104358979">Although I've read this before it was still a good book to re-read. There is so much history of New Orleans written, with about the first 700 pages mostly detailing the background of the Mayfair witches. The main characters are Rowan Mayfair and Michael curry, with the ghost Lasher.<br /><br />Although long at just over 1200 pages, the book is never slow moveing. The characters are interesting, and with some you really like. Lots of the very large Mayfair family are great such as Beartrice, but in Carlotta their was what seemed to be pure evil.<br /><br />Rowan thinks she can control Lasher, but she is so wrong. Instead of getting Aaron and the Talamasca, which is an order of people who have dedicated their lives to the study of the paranormal, and the family to help her she takes the ghost on and things go wrong. <br />The book is one I can recommend to anyone who loves Anne rice, it doesn't disappoint.</span>

Some of the characters I wanted to read more of but she would go to another one I didn't care so much about. If you are an Anne Rice fan, then take the plunge and read it, if you are looking for a good read, then skip this one.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sfJWx8c/Zs8ns5EQBsfYynOZzfuxPEYVyBTq+X7vBRjUJmkUNe1yNatr5at4pj54Om4O4vjhAb+iHe9rsnrzXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/sVq0zWOYraoNGr2+WbMqm3L9NrFK3BphvkynNkQTbKbEVUAx1x2TCTsHk2HByoYJDw3w4z2N8Ps8DcOFYW79w==')})

Resonant with supernatural suspense, mesmerizing eroticism, and lush detail, The Witching Hour, Lasher, and Taltos have bewitched the imaginations of readers everywhere. Now comes the definitive touchstone guide to the history and mystery of this magnificent dynasty of witches.Just as she did with The Vampire Companion, biographer and Anne Rice authority Katherine Ramsland presents a fascinating A-to-Z encyclopedia of information, interpretation, and analysis--this time devoted to the characters and key events, places and symbols, historical and mythological themes of the Lives of the Mayfair Witches novels. Created with the full cooperation of Anne Rice, The Witches\' Companion features detailed character breakdowns, from the present-day enchantress Rowan Mayfair to the lustful spirit Lasher; a complete genealogy of the Mayfair family; a chronology of events; a guide to geographical locations; the intriguing origins of the Mayfairs\' extraordinary clan; revealing observations from Anne Rice herself; and much more.Illustrated throughout with hundreds of photos, drawings, and maps, The Witches\' Companion will be every Anne Rice fan\'s inseparable companion in traveling through the unforgettable     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><img alt="7577" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p2/7577.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer256331972759247122">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText256331972759247122">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="256331972759247122">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Anne Rice...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/2926133-the-witching-hour">Trivia About The Witching Hour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

        </div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2926133-the-witching-hour">Quotes from The Witching Hour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Give me a man or woman who has read a thousand books and you give me an interesting companion. Give me a man or woman who has read perhaps three and you give me a very dangerous enemy indeed.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/109946-give-me-a-man-or-woman-who-has-read-a" class="actionLinkLite">635 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I believe in Free Will, the Force Almighty by which we conduct ourselves as if we were the sons and daughters of a just and wise God, even if there is no such Supreme Being. And by free will, we can choose to do good on this earth, no matter that we all die, and do not know where we go when we die, or if a justice or explanation awaits us.<br /> I believe that we can, through our reason, know what good is, and in the communion of men and women, in which the forgiveness of wrongs will always be more significant than the avenging of them, and that in the beautiful natural world that surrounds us, we represent the best and the finest of beings, for we alone can see that natural beauty, appreciate it, learn from it, weep for it, and seek to conserve it and protect it.<br /> I believe finally that we are the only true moral force in the physical world, the makers of, ethics and moral ideas, and that we must be as good as the gods we created in the past to guide us. <br /> I believe that through our finest efforts, we will succeed finally in creating heaven on earth, and we do it every time that we love, every time that we embrace, every time that we commit to create rather than destroy, every time that we place life over death, and the natural over what is unnatural, insofar as we are able to define it.<br /> And I suppose I do believe in the final analysis that a peace of mind can be obtained in the face of the worst horrors and the worst losses. It can be obtained by faith in change and in will and in accident and by faith in ourselves, that we will do the right thing, more often than not, in the face of adversity.<br /> For ours is the power and the glory, because we are capable of visions and ideas which are ultimately stronger and more enduring than we are.<br /> That is my credo. That is my belief, for what it's worth, and it sustains me. And if I were to die right now, I wouldn't be afraid. Because I can't believe that horror or chaos awaits us.<br /> If any revelation awaits us at all, it must be as good as our ideals and our philosophy. For surely nature must embrace the visible and the invisible, and it couldn't fall short of us. The thing that makes the flowers open and the snowflakes fall must contain a wisdom and a final secret as intricate and beautiful as the blooming camellia or the clouds gathering above, so white and so pure in the blackness.<br /> If that isn't so, then we are in the grip of a staggering irony. And all the spooks of hell might as well dance. There could be a devil. People who burn other people to death are fine. There could be anything. <br /> But the world is simply to beautiful for that.<br /> At least it seems that way to me.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/702913-i-believe-in-free-will-the-force-almighty-by-which" class="actionLinkLite">16 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/2926133-the-witching-hour" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
